[2026-01-05T20:11:18Z] Abhishek Vats: Q. Y was the term Nikola Tesla used for what we now call X-rays. While Wilhelm Röntgen is officially credited with their discovery in 1895, Tesla was experimenting with this "invisible radiant energy" as early as 1894. ↵ Tesla didn't just stumble upon X-rays; he developed a unique system to produce them that differed from the standard methods of the time. Unlike other scientists who used standard batteries, Tesla used his Tesla Coil to produce high-frequency, high-voltage currents. He designed specialized "single-electrode" vacuum tubes. These were more powerful than the Crookes tubes used by his peers, allowing him to take images from much further away—up to 8 feet. His images were startlingly clear. His most famous Y is an 1896 image of his own foot inside a shoe, which clearly showed the bones as well as the metal nails and eyelets of the footwear. Id Y? ‎<This message was edited>
